2:27:1738:0:14:72:311:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Dynamic Demand Estimation in Auction Markets
2:28:1782:14:14:72:249:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Matthew Backus and Gregory Lewis
2:29:1814:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 22375
2:30:1842:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:June 2016
2:31:1851:14:28:72:175:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. C57,D44,L0
2:32:1869:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:33:1877:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Economists  have  developed  empirically  tractable  demand  systems  for  fixed  price  markets.  In 
2:34:1979:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:contrast, empirical   auction   techniques   treat   each   auction   in   isolation,   ignoring   market 
2:35:2084:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:interactions.  We  provide a  framework  for  estimating  demand  in  a  large  auction  market  with  a 
2:36:2188:14:14:71:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:dynamic  population  of  buyers with  unit  demand  and  heterogeneous  preferences  over  a  finite  set 
2:37:2293:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:of  differentiated  products.  We  offer an  empirically  tractable  equilibrium  concept  under  which 
2:38:2396:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:bidders behave as though they are in a steady-state, characterize bidding, and prove existence of 
2:39:2493:14:14:71:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:equilibrium. Having developed a demand system, we show that it is non-parametrically identified 
2:40:2588:14:14:71:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:from  panel  data,  and  that  this  result  is  robust  to  typical data  limitations,  reserve  prices,  random 
2:41:2701:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:coefficient  demand,  public  signals  that  refine  beliefs  about market  conditions,  unobserved 
2:42:2800:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:heterogeneity, idiosyncratic preferences, and random latent outside options. We apply the model 
2:43:2895:14:14:72:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:to estimate demand and measure consumer surplus in the market for compact cameras on eBay. 
2:44:2985:14:14:72:546:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Our analysis highlights the importance of both dynamic bidding strategies and panel data sample 
2:45:3080:14:42:72:297:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:selection issues when analyzing these markets.
2:46:3126:42:14:72:153:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Matthew Backus
2:47:3140:14:14:72:211:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:Graduate School of Business
2:48:3167:14:14:72:173:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:Columbia University
2:49:3186:14:14:72:220:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:3022 Broadway, Uris Hall 619
2:50:3214:14:14:72:179:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:New York, NY 10027
2:51:3232:14:14:72:124:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:52:3240:14:28:72:226:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:matthew.backus@columbia.edu
2:53:3267:28:14:72:144:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Gregory Lewis
2:54:3280:14:14:72:235:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:Microsoft Research New England
2:55:3310:14:14:72:159:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:1 Memorial Drive
2:56:3326:14:14:72:184:224:12:Times:12:Times:C:Cambridge, MA 02142
2:57:3345:14:14:72:124:210:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:58:3353:14:0:72:184:196:12:Times:12:Times:C:glewis@microsoft.com
3:59:3373:0:36:72:208:671:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:60:3390:36:18:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Most  goods  and  services  are  sold  at  fixed  prices.   Yet  auctions  are  used  as  the  allocation
3:61:3495:18:18:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism in a wide variety of contexts, including procurement contracts, treasury bills and
3:62:3587:18:18:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the granting of oil drilling and spectrum rights.  Technology companies such as Facebook,
3:63:3676:18:18:72:540:581:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Google and Microsoft sell advertisers access to online consumers through display and search
3:64:3767:18:18:72:540:563:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advertising auctions.  And though the majority of eBay’s revenue now comes from fixed price
3:65:3858:18:18:72:540:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:listings of new goods,  they still sell a large number of goods (both in absolute and dollar
3:66:3950:18:24:72:166:527:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terms) by auction.
3:67:3968:24:18:72:540:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:These markets share many common features.  Buyers get multiple purchase opportunities
3:68:4053:18:18:72:540:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over time, either for exactly the same product (e.g.  in search advertising where a product
3:69:4144:18:18:72:540:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is a keyword), or for close substitutes (e.g.  in treasury bill auctions).  This allows bidders to
3:70:4242:18:18:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intertemporally substitute, making participation and bidding decisions in light of the option
3:71:4335:18:18:72:540:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value  of  waiting  for  future  purchasing  opportunities.   Both  bids  and  participation  choices
3:72:4436:18:18:72:540:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will  reflect  individual-specific  preferences  over  the  heterogeneous  products  available.   For
3:73:4537:18:18:72:540:395:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:example,  in  highway  procurement,  Lewis  and  Bajari  (2011)  document  matching  between
3:74:4629:18:18:72:540:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contractors and contract based primarily on distance and contract size, while in online labor
3:75:4722:18:18:72:540:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:markets,  employers are more likely to award contracts to workers from their own country
3:76:4810:18:24:72:226:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Krasnokutskaya et al., 2016).
3:77:4840:24:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  the  fixed  price  context,  an  influential  discrete  choice  demand  estimation  approach  has
3:78:4941:18:18:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:been developed that models how buyers with unit demand and heterogeneous preferences
3:79:5025:18:18:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decide which goods to purchase (e.g.  Berry (1994), Berry et al. (1995), Gowrisankaran and
3:80:5115:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rysman (2009)).  However, until recently, there has been no analogous work in the empirical
3:81:5206:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auctions literature, which has generally focused on the analysis of a repeated cross-section
3:82:5298:18:24:72:487:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of static auctions for identical products.  The goal of this paper is to fill this gap.
3:83:5385:24:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A “whole-market” approach that incorporates dynamics and product differentiation can be
3:84:5472:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:important  for  policy  counterfactuals.   For  example,  in  setting  optimal  reserves,  a  static
3:85:5572:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model of second-price sealed bid auctions would suggest that when a monopolist changes her
3:86:5662:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserve price policy, she should expect no change in buyer behavior (it is weakly dominant
3:87:5752:18:18:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for a buyer to bid their valuation regardless).  By contrast, in our dynamic setting, a new
3:88:5843:18:19:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserve  price  policy  will  affect  buyer’s  continuation  values,  and  therefore  bids  throughout
3:89:5945:19:18:72:540:94:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the marketplace.  Reserve prices will also have an effect on the endogenous set of incumbent
3:90:6037:18:0:72:540:76:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidders.  And without taking product differentiation seriously, we cannot use auction data to
4:91:6131:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:say much about cross-price elasticities, or how an increase in the supply of one good would
4:92:6222:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affect the transaction prices of other goods (see Newberry (2015) for evidence that increased
4:93:6315:18:24:72:243:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:supply depresses prices on eBay).
4:94:6348:24:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The present paper analyzes a model that is very closely related to the above work on fixed
4:95:6438:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price  markets,  but  with  a  data-generating  process  that  is  given  by  equilibrium  play  in  a
4:96:6540:18:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic auction market.  Vis-`a-vis that literature, our approach is analogous to the second-
4:97:6633:18:18:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:choice  demand  estimation  approach  of  Berry  et  al.  (2004)  because  we  use  bids  placed  by
4:98:6733:18:18:72:540:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same bidder on different products.  This is informative about thejointdistribution of
4:99:6822:18:19:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:valuations  or,  in  the  parlance  of  the  fixed-price  market  literature,  cross-elasticities.   The
4:100:6926:19:18:72:540:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction format also allows us to credibly identify a region of the distribution of valuations
4:101:7019:18:18:72:540:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  we  often  struggle  with:  the  right  tail.   This  region  can  be  hard  to  identify  in  fixed–
4:102:7126:18:18:72:540:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price markets because of limited variation in characteristics (in particular, prices);  for the
4:103:7221:18:18:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subset of buyers whose choice behavior doesn’t change over the support of observed prices,
4:104:7311:18:18:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identification is entirely parametric.  To put it more succinctly, we can’t invert an inequality,
4:105:7408:18:24:72:190:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but we can invert bids.
4:106:7431:24:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here  we  offer  what  we  hope  is  a  comprehensive  analysis  of  our  model:   we  characterize
4:107:7530:18:18:72:540:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:participation and bidding decisions, prove existence of equilibrium, offer a number of non-
4:108:7621:18:18:72:540:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parametric identification results, and apply the model to measure consumer surplus in the
4:109:7710:18:18:72:540:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market for compact cameras on eBay.  Along the way, we deal with many of the method-
4:110:7794:18:23:72:455:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ological issues that are likely to arise in similar models of auction markets.
4:111:7872:23:19:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Specifically, we consider a model of repeated second-price auctions of differentiated products,
4:112:7967:19:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  which  buyers  with  unit  demand  and  heterogeneous,  perfectly  persistent  and  privately
4:113:8064:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:known multidimensional valuations for a finite set of types of good must work out when to
4:114:8153:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:participate and how much to bid.  Persistence of preferences is a realistic feature of many
4:115:8244:18:18:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction markets, but causes game theoretic problems that do not arise in fixed price markets.
4:116:8337:18:18:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:So-called “leakage effects” are a particular concern, whereby a bidder’s bid today may reveal
4:117:8430:18:18:72:540:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their valuation to other bidders, affecting the evolution of future play (this remains true even
4:118:8526:18:18:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when other bidders cannot observe rival bids; less information just implies a harder filtration
4:119:8621:18:24:72:325:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:problem for the bidders and the outside analyst).
4:120:8670:24:18:72:540:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:When markets are “small” (in the sense that there are few bidders in the market), the ap-
4:121:8759:18:18:72:540:106:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proach of the dynamic games literature has been to simply assume that everything persistent
4:122:8850:18:0:72:540:88:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is commonly known, and that all private shocks are iid (see e.g.  Jofre-Bonet and Pesendorfer
5:123:8944:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2003), Aguirregabiria and Mira (2007), Bajari et al. (2007), Pakes et al. (2007); Fershtman
5:124:9036:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Pakes  (2012)  is  a  recent  exception).   But  in  “large”  markets  (i.e.   many  anonymous
5:125:9135:18:18:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidders), it is attractive to instead assume that players form beliefs about their rivals in a
5:126:9229:18:19:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simpler way.  Here we assume that bidders simply take the distribution of rival bids for each
5:127:9322:19:18:72:540:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:product as given and optimize against this, forming neither more refined beliefs (by condi-
5:128:9413:18:18:72:540:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tioning on other information available to them) nor considering the possibility of trying to
5:129:9505:18:18:72:540:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:manipulate the evolution of this distribution with their bid.  An equilibrium is a fixed point
5:130:9599:18:18:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in which bidders optimize given their beliefs about rival bids, and those beliefs are consistent
5:131:9695:18:18:72:540:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the long run time-averages of equilibrium play, i.e.  the stationary distribution.  This is
5:132:9791:18:18:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar to ideas elsewhere in the literature, such as the model of belief formation in Krusell
5:133:9885:18:18:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Smith  (1998)  and  the  oblivious  /  mean-field  equilibrium  concept  of  Weintraub  et  al.
5:134:9985:18:24:72:221:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2008) and Iyer et al. (2014).
5:135:10015:24:18:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In equilibrium, losing bidders “win” the opportunity to play the game again tomorrow.  The
5:136:10105:18:18:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimal strategy requires that bidders bid their valuation less their continuation value when-
5:137:10199:18:18:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ever this is positive, and otherwise not participate.  A bidder’s valuation is thus identified
5:138:10293:18:18:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by adding their bid to their continuation value.  In other words, to estimate demand, one
5:139:10382:18:18:72:540:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:must  estimate  continuation  values.   We  show  that  these  can  be  learned  from  observing  a
5:140:10481:18:18:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidder’s “pseudo-type” — their optimal bid on each product — as well as the distributions
5:141:10570:18:24:72:347:340:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:of competing bids and the exit and supply processes.1
5:142:10623:24:18:72:540:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  existence  of  an  inversion  from  bids  to  types  is  often  sufficient  to  prove  identification
5:143:10729:18:18:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  static  auctions  (e.g.   Guerre  et  al.  (2000),  Athey  and  Haile  (2007)):  when  each  bidder
5:144:10832:18:18:72:540:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids  exactly  once,  the  distribution  of  pseudo-types  is  just  the  distribution  of  bids,  which
5:145:10936:18:18:72:540:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is observed.  But when bidders bid multiple times, they may win (an therefore exit) before
5:146:11026:18:18:72:540:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recording a “complete,” or invertible, history consisting of a bid on every product (i.e.  before
5:147:11123:18:18:72:540:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their  pseudo-type  is  known).   The  probability  of  reaching  a  complete  history  varies  with
5:148:11223:18:18:72:540:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:type, so we need to correct for selection in measuring the distribution of pseudo-types.  By
5:149:11315:18:18:72:540:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:combining  this  new  selection  correction  idea  with  the  familiar  inversion  approach,  we  are
5:150:11416:18:18:72:540:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:able to bound demand.  Our identification result is pointwise up to the set of bidders who
5:151:11506:18:24:72:288:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prefer not to participate in some auctions.
5:152:11549:24:18:72:540:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  subsequent  sections,  we  extend  the  model  to  cases  with  limited  data,  reserve  prices,
5:153:11649:18:15:85:539:112:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:1A common refrain in the empirical auctions literature is that losers’ payoffs are “normalized to zero.”
5:154:11753:15:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:We view this as a strong assumption, rather than a normalization.  In our model the continuation value that
5:155:11860:12:0:72:540:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:bidders anticipate when they lose is not constant across bidders, but instead depends on their private type.
6:156:11969:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:random coefficient demand, public signals that refine beliefs about market conditions, unob-
6:157:12061:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:served heterogeneity, idiosyncratic preferences and random latent outside options.  Most of
6:158:12152:18:18:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these extensions are reasonably straightforward given the tools developed earlier, as well as
6:159:12245:18:19:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results on deconvolution used in Li and Vuong (1998) and Krasnokutskaya (2011).  The main
6:160:12334:19:18:72:540:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exception is the case with outside options and endogenous exit, which is harder.  There we
6:161:12424:18:18:72:540:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show that observable differences in the exit rate across bidders imply a first order separable
6:162:12518:18:23:72:504:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differential equation that can be used to identify differences in their outside options.
6:163:12606:23:18:72:540:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The final section of the paper applies this framework to data from eBay’s compact camera
6:164:12694:18:19:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market.  We document that substitution over time and across cameras with different levels of
6:165:12786:19:18:72:540:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:resolution occurs in this market, and that there is both observable and unobservable hetero-
6:166:12878:18:18:72:540:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:geneity within cameras of a given resolution.  We model preferences as a linear combination
6:167:12969:18:18:72:540:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a random taste for a camera and a random taste for camera resolution, and estimate the
6:168:13058:18:18:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of these random coefficients.  We show that our estimated model is able to match
6:169:13151:18:18:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the data well, and then use it to calculate consumer surplus.  We find that consumer surplus
6:170:13243:18:18:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is twice as large as we would have estimated had we ignored continuation values, $6.04 per
6:171:13333:18:18:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidder rather than $2.73.  We chose the application for its expositional value rather than any
6:172:13427:18:18:72:540:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy implications:  it gives us the opportunity to show how our methodology can be im-
6:173:13515:18:18:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plemented with limited data; how it fares under unobserved heterogeneity, and to illustrate
6:174:13606:18:40:72:492:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that dynamics and substitution are important for understanding auction markets.
6:175:13685:40:19:72:539:300:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Literature  Review.The  paper  is  related  to  various  strands  of  literature.   Jofre-Bonet
6:176:13780:19:18:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Pesendorfer (2003) was the first paper to attack estimation in a dynamic auction game.
6:177:13870:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Subsequent to this, a number of papers have looked at dynamics on the eBay platform specif-
6:178:13961:18:18:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically.  Budish (2008) examines the optimality of eBay’s market design with respect to the
6:179:14051:18:18:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sequencing of sales and information revelation.  In Said (2009), the author investigates effi-
6:180:14145:18:18:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ciency and revenue maximization in a similar setup through the lens of dynamic mechanism
6:181:14233:18:18:72:540:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:design.   Zeithammer  (2006)  developed  a  model  with  forward-looking  bidders,  and  showed
6:182:14328:18:18:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both theoretically and empirically that bidders shade down current bids in response to the
6:183:14418:18:18:72:540:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:presence of upcoming auctions of similar objects.  Ingster (2009) develops a dynamic model
6:184:14508:18:18:72:540:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of auctions of identical objects, and provides equilibrium characterization and identification
6:185:14602:18:18:72:540:119:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results.   Sailer  (2006)  estimates  participation  costs  for  bidders  facing  an  infinite  sequence
6:186:14706:18:18:72:540:101:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of identical auctions.  Nekipelov (2007) analyzes a model where bidders attempt to prevent
6:187:14796:18:0:72:540:83:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:learning by late bidding, while Hopenhayn and Saeedi (2016) develop and estimate a model
7:188:14885:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in which bidder’s bidding opportunities and valuations evolve dynamically within an auc-
7:189:14973:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion according to a Markov process.  Bodoh-Creed et al. (2013) employ our methodology in
7:190:15061:18:18:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analyzing the optimal fee structure for the eBay platform.  Hendricks and Sorensen (2014)
7:191:15150:18:19:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:offer a model, similar to our own but in continuous time and with a single product type, and
7:192:15242:19:23:72:348:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analyze the efficiency of the eBay trading mechanism.
7:193:15295:23:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Relative  to  this  literature,  our  main  contribution  is  the  focus  on  sequential  auctions  of
7:194:15397:18:18:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneous  objects,  where  bidders  have  multidimensional persistent  private  valuations.
7:195:15493:18:18:72:540:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In short, we are focused on developing a demand system.  This is also a topic of interest in
7:196:15585:18:19:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other recent papers.  Adams (2009) examines the problem of nonparametric identification
7:197:15672:19:18:72:540:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when differentiated products are sold by simultaneous auction,  and Krasnokutskaya et al.
7:198:15761:18:18:72:540:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2014) develop a model of participation and bidding in an online labor market.  Our paper
7:199:15850:18:18:72:540:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differs from these papers in allowing buyers to participate repeatedly and dealing with the
7:200:15941:18:18:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic  issues  this  creates.   One  of  the  advantages  of  using  a  dynamic  model  is  that  we
7:201:16043:18:18:72:540:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  able  to  make  use  of  panel  data  in  estimation,  rather  than  treating  it  as  a  repeated
7:202:16146:18:40:72:446:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cross-section, which allows identification of individual bidder preferences.
7:203:16222:40:18:72:539:372:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Paper Structure.The paper proceeds as follows.  In the next section we introduce the
7:204:16306:18:18:72:540:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:basic model, and prove existence of and characterize equilibrium.  Sections 3 and 4 discuss
7:205:16397:18:18:72:540:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-parametric identification of the basic model and a series of extensions. Section 5 presents
7:206:16492:18:51:72:290:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our application, while Section 6 concludes.
7:207:16535:51:36:72:377:267:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Model and Equilibrium Analysis
7:208:16570:36:18:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  consider  a  market  in  which  competing  products  are  sold  by  second-price  sealed  bid
7:209:16667:18:18:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auctions.  These auctions are held in discrete time, with either zero or one good auctioned
7:210:16758:18:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:per period over an infinite horizon.  Since our focus is on demand, we assume for simplicity
7:211:16850:18:18:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that supply is random and exogenous.  Bidders have unit demand, and enter the market with
7:212:16939:18:18:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:private and perfectly persistent valuations for each of the objects.  They are inattentive, and
7:213:17034:18:18:72:540:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  active  in  any  particular  period  with  constant  probability.   When  active,  they  choose
7:214:17134:18:18:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whether or not to participate in the current auction, and how much to bid.  We show that
7:215:17222:18:19:72:540:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they bid their valuation less their continuation value, and assume they assess the latter based
7:216:17317:19:0:72:540:86:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the steady-state distribution of supply and competing bids, rather than on current market
8:217:17410:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditions (e.g.  the number of competing bidders in the current auction).  Winning bidders
8:218:17501:18:24:72:493:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exit the market with certainty, while losing bidders exit with constant probability.
8:219:17585:24:18:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  have  chosen  this  set  of  assumptions  to  match  some  features  of  the  market  for  digital
8:220:17687:18:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cameras on eBay, which is our empirical application.  In any eBay category (such as digital
8:221:17778:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cameras), there are many different products sold by auction to a large number of anonymous
8:222:17868:18:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:buyers.2Although these auctions typically last for many days, and thus overlap — so that
8:223:17956:18:18:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at any given point in time there are many auctions occurring simultaneously — they finish
8:224:18045:18:18:72:540:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at different ending times, in sequence.  As Bajari and Horta ̧csu (2004) and Hendricks and
8:225:18135:18:19:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Porter  (2007)  have  noted,  this  timing,  combined  with  the  way  the  proxy  bidding  system
8:226:18233:19:44:72:540:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:works, imply that eBay is well approximated as sequence of second-price sealed bid auctions.
8:227:18325:44:32:72:200:458:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Environment
8:228:18343:32:40:72:437:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We formalize the above description of the environment in what follows:
8:229:18413:40:18:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Supply.There areJdistinct kinds of goods sold in a market, indexed byj= 1...J.  We
8:230:18495:18:18:71:539:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denote the set of products byJ.  In each periodt, a good may be available for purchase.
8:231:18582:18:18:71:539:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Supply  is  exogenous  and  Markov,  with  the  current  productjtdrawn  from  a  stationary
8:232:18674:18:18:71:539:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multinomial distribution conditional on the lagged productjt−1.  We allow for the possibility
8:233:18767:18:19:71:539:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that no product is available in a given period, and so supply can be summarized by a square
8:234:18858:19:18:71:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transition matrixQof sizeJ+ 1×J+ 1, where the entryQj,kgives the probability product
8:235:18942:18:18:71:539:277:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:kwill be supplied next whenjis currently offered (and the last row and column give the
8:236:19028:18:18:71:539:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cases where no product is offered now and will be offered later, respectively).  We assume
8:237:19118:18:18:71:539:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:moreover that the multinomials have full support, so that regardless of what was supplied
8:238:19207:18:18:71:539:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:att−1, it is possible that any of theJproducts (or nothing) is supplied att.  When a good
8:239:19296:18:40:71:360:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is available, it is sold by second-price sealed-bid auction.
8:240:19356:40:18:71:539:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Demand.At the beginning of each period,Etbuyers enter the market, whereEtis sampled
8:241:19439:18:18:71:539:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:independently over time from a distributionFEwith support{0,1,2...E}.  Each buyer has
8:242:19524:18:18:72:540:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unit demand,  and has aperfectly  persistentvalue for each of the goods summarized by a
8:243:19611:18:18:72:539:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:privately known vector of valuationsx= (x1,x2···xJ)∈RJ.  This value is drawn iid across
8:244:19698:18:18:72:539:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:buyers on entry according to a distributionFwith strictly positive density over its support
8:245:19789:18:0:85:474:75:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:A:2eBay hides the identity of the bidders by replacing parts of the username with asterisks.
9:246:19880:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:X= [0,x]J.  The new entrants combine with the population of buyers from previous periods
9:247:19968:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to form a cohort of bidders of sizeNt.  To ensure that the maximum number of buyersNis
9:248:20054:18:24:72:401:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bounded, we assume that whenNt=N, no-one enters (Et= 0).
9:249:20110:24:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:New entrants are always active; the remaining incumbent members of the cohort are active
9:250:20198:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in each period with iid chanceτ.  Active buyers participate in the current auction (if one
9:251:20288:18:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is held), observing the product currently under auction, and placing a weakly positive bid
9:252:20378:18:18:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:b∈R+.   We  assume  that  the  good  sells  only  if  the  highest  bid  isstrictlypositive,  so  a
9:253:20477:18:18:71:539:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:buyer can always opt-out of an auction by bidding zero.  Agents are risk-neutral and have
9:254:20566:18:19:71:539:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quasi-linear utility, receiving a total payoff ofxj−pfor buying a goodjat pricep, and zero
9:255:20656:19:18:71:539:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:otherwise.  If an auction is held and a bidder wins the auction, they exit the market.  All
9:256:20747:18:18:71:540:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other active bidders exit with probability (1−r) (i.e.r∈(0,1) is the survival rate).  Inactive
9:257:20841:18:18:71:539:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidders do not exit.  We assume that agents do not discount future payoffs,  although the
9:258:20930:18:18:71:539:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exogenous  exit  probability  effectively  leads  to  discounting.   We  discuss  bidder  beliefs  and
9:259:21032:18:45:71:222:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strategies in the next section.
9:260:21063:45:31:71:167:385:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.2    Analysis
9:261:21078:31:18:71:539:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We begin our analysis by looking at the buyer’s incentives.  In our application to the compact
9:262:21172:18:18:71:539:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:camera market on eBay, it seems reasonable to assume that buyers have simple models of
9:263:21258:18:18:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the competition they face.  We formalize this idea by assuming that bidders believe that the
9:264:21350:18:18:71:539:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of the highest competing bid is equal to the historical average and best respond
9:265:21443:18:18:71:539:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accordingly  (this  assumption  or  some  variant  is  implicitly  used  in  the  existing  literature
9:266:21545:18:18:71:539:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Ingster, 2009; Hendricks and Sorensen, 2014)).  LetB1jbe a random variable denoting the
9:267:21633:18:28:71:521:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:highest bid in an auction for goodj, and letG1jbe its cumulative distribution function.
9:268:21720:28:18:71:540:218:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Assumption 1(Beliefs about competing bids).Following any history of play, bidders
9:269:21801:18:34:71:466:200:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:believe that the highest rival bid in an auction for goodjhas distributionG1j.
9:270:21879:34:18:71:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is a sensible way for bidders to form beliefs, though it is non-standard.  Agents in games
9:271:21974:18:18:71:539:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are usually modeled as Bayesian, and so would condition on the recent bidding history and
9:272:22063:18:18:71:539:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:any other observables in their information set (e.g.  the number of competing bidders in the
9:273:22155:18:18:71:539:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:current auction) to update their prior and form a posterior over the current distribution of
9:274:22247:18:18:71:539:94:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:types  in  the  market.3We  have  elected  to  model  bidder  beliefs  in  this  way  both  because
9:275:22346:18:0:85:539:76:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:3Even if this data was hidden a bidder could learn from their own experience over time (e.g.  a bidder
10:276:22449:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it  substantively  simplifies  the  game  theory,  and  because  the  gap  between  the  behavior  of
10:277:22550:18:24:72:502:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sophisticated Bayesian bidders and those that obey assumption 1 is probably small.
10:278:22632:24:18:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Just as information about competitor valuations has no effect on the optimal bid in a static
10:279:22724:18:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:second-price auction, knowing the current distribution of types in the market is useful only
10:280:22816:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  extent  that  it  predictsfuturecompetition,  which  determines  continuation  values.
10:281:22911:18:18:71:539:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Since bidders participate only intermittently and eBay is a large market with high turnover
10:282:23002:18:18:71:539:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  market  participants,  current  market  conditions  have  little  predictive  power  for  future
10:283:23102:18:18:71:539:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:competition.  Assumption 1 is thus a good approximation to the behavior of Bayesian bidders
10:284:23193:18:19:71:539:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this marketplace, though the model can be extended to weaken this assumption and allow
10:285:23282:19:23:71:396:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidders to condition on other state variables (see section 4.3.2).
10:286:23348:23:18:71:539:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Under this assumption, the only payoff relevant-information in each period is the bidder’s
10:287:23438:18:18:71:539:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:type and the current object under auction (we show this below).  So without loss of generality
10:288:23532:18:18:71:539:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a pure strategy is just a vectorβ:X →RJ, a bid on each product as a function of type, with
10:289:23622:18:18:72:539:425:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:jth coordinateβj.  Moreover, letμβj(·) denote the ergodic measure of the first-order statistic
10:290:23716:18:19:72:540:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of bids, which depends onβ.4We can think of this measure as capturing the time-average
10:291:23802:19:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we would compute if we picked aβand simulated the market for an arbitrarily long time.
10:292:23888:18:18:72:540:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We are now in a position to define what it means for the market to be in equilibrium (subject

10:295:24095:33:28:82:488:291:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:(Optimality)βe(x)is a best response for typexgiven beliefs{G1j(b)}j∈J, and
10:296:24169:28:0:73:279:263:12:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f10:C:(Consistency)  for everyj,G1j(b) =μβ

10:299:24215:31:18:72:540:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The definition mirrors the requirements for a Bayes–Nash equilibrium: play must be optimal
10:300:24305:18:18:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given beliefs, and beliefs must be consistent with play. The consistency requirement explicitly
10:301:24400:18:18:72:540:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:connects beliefs, as specified by Assumption 1, to the distribution of the highest bid on each

10:303:24532:22:12:72:540:153:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:who lost yesterday might reason that competition was fierce yesterday,  and may still be so today).  This
10:304:24637:12:12:72:540:141:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:gives rise to a winner’s curse effect (Budish, 2008).  There is some evidence that this kind of learning occurs
10:305:24748:12:12:72:540:129:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:on eBay:  Coey et al. (2015) show that bidders tend to (modestly) increase their bids in subsequent auctions
10:306:24856:12:8:72:441:117:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:for the same product, although they attribute this to deadlines rather than learning.
10:307:24941:8:15:85:540:109:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:4In an earlier version of this paper, we proved that for anyβ, such an ergodic measure exists, is unique

11:310:25218:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We can now specify the buyer’s decision problem.  It is dynamic, since losers may have an

12:354:27485:15:14:72:540:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1 in a two-dimensional example.  In panel 1(a) the two functions represent optimal bids on
12:355:27575:14:15:72:540:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:product 1 as a function of bidders’ valuations for good 1, fixing their valuation for good 2.
12:356:27668:15:14:72:540:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Panel 1(b) represents three exemplary bidders:  their types{x,x′,x′′}and their associated
12:357:27757:14:36:72:288:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids{b,b′,b′′}.  See the text for discussion.
12:358:27802:36:18:72:540:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In static second price auctions, bidders bid their values so that they are indifferent between
12:359:27896:18:19:72:540:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginally winning (paying their bid, earning zero surplus) and marginally losing (earning
12:360:27986:19:18:72:540:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero surplus).  The same logic applies here:  bidders must be indifferent between marginally
12:361:28078:18:18:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:winning and losing, and since losers receive their continuation value, bids must be equal to
12:362:28170:18:18:72:540:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value less continuation value.  It is possible that a bidder prefers to wait for a product they
12:363:28265:18:18:72:540:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value more highly rather than win the current object at a price of zero, in which case opting
12:364:28358:18:23:72:305:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out of the auction by bidding zero is optimal.
12:365:28404:23:19:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The assumption that bids are either zero or interior to the support of{G1j}j∈Jis necessary
12:366:28494:19:18:72:539:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for uniqueness,  since if there is an interval [b,b′] on which rival bids are unsupported and
12:367:28587:18:18:72:540:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the putatively unique best response falls in this range, any other bid in the range will also
12:368:28680:18:18:72:540:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be a best response.  Note that the characterization in (2) is implicit — i.e.,vj(x) is defined
12:369:28774:18:18:72:540:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recursively  according  to  the  Bellman  equation  in  (1)  —  but  since  the  value  functions  in
12:370:28875:18:18:72:540:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Markov Decision Problems are unique (Stokey et al., 1989), the characterization of optimal
12:371:28965:18:18:72:540:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids as valuations less continuation values immediately delivers uniqueness of{βj(x)}(i.e.
12:372:29055:18:18:72:540:118:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that they are functions).  Continuity follows from the continuity of payoffs in types.  Mono-
12:373:29148:18:18:72:540:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tonicity is natural:  if a bidder values objectjmore, they optimally increase their bid for it,
12:374:29243:18:0:72:406:82:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and correspondingly shade their bids on substitute objects down.
13:375:29309:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We offer some graphical intuition for the bidding strategies of Lemma 1 in Figure 1 with a
13:376:29399:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two-dimensional example.  Panel 1(a) depicts the monotonicity properties of optimal bids.
13:377:29488:18:18:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The more a bidder values product 1 the more she bids on it.  However, bidders with higher
13:378:29577:18:19:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:valuations also shade more; a bidder’s continuation value is monotone increasing in her value
13:379:29670:19:18:72:540:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for product 1,  which induces the concavity of the function.  Increases in her valuation for
13:380:29762:18:18:72:540:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:product 2 cause a level shift, and may even drive non–participation ifx1is small — orx2is
13:381:29851:18:18:72:540:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:large — enough.  Panel 1(b) depicts three conjectured bidder types (x, x’, and x”) and their
13:382:29943:18:18:72:540:544:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corresponding bids (b, b’, and b” respectively).  The bidder of typexhas a high valuation
13:383:30032:18:18:72:540:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for both products and therefore shades both of her bids substantially.  The bidder of type
13:384:30122:18:18:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:x′gets the same high utility from product 1, but zero utility from product 2.  Therefore she
13:385:30214:18:18:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not participate in auctions of product 2; she prefers to wait for auctions of product 1.
13:386:30307:18:18:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, the bidder of typex′′is unlikely to win in either state of the world, and therefore
13:387:30399:18:28:72:379:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shades her bid very little, but participates in both auctions.
13:388:30461:28:18:72:539:426:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Theorem 1(Existence).A pure strategy equilibrium exists in which strategies are charac-
13:389:30548:18:18:72:540:408:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:F:terized by Lemma 1.  WhenJ= 1, there is a unique equilibrium within the class of strategies
13:390:30639:18:34:72:209:390:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:characterized by Lemma 1.
13:391:30664:34:18:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  proof  is  non-trivial.   We  must  find  a  fixed  point  in  strategy-space:   the  equilibrium
13:392:30766:18:18:72:540:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strategiesβemust be a best response to the distributions{G1j}, i.e.  the ergodic distributions
13:393:30860:18:18:72:539:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the highest competing bid on each product generated byβeand the entry, supply and exit
13:394:30949:18:18:72:540:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:processes.  To show that such a strategyβeexists, we apply Schauder’s fixed point theorem
13:395:31038:18:18:72:539:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the space of continuous functions on the type spaceX.  Doing so requires some functional
13:396:31129:18:18:72:540:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis.  In the appendix we show that the set of best responses to any continuous bidding
13:397:31220:18:18:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function is uniformly equicontinuous and bounded (a compactness condition), and that the
13:398:31308:18:24:72:488:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:best response varies smoothly with the bidding function (a continuity condition).
13:399:31389:24:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The case with a single product (J= 1) is easier, and we can prove uniqueness of equilibrium.
13:400:31481:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is because the types are totally ordered and monotone bidding preserves that ordering,
13:401:31572:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so that the chance of winning an auction is entirely pinned down by a bidder’s type.  As a
13:402:31662:18:18:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:result who wins and who loses can be determined without knowing the equilibrium bidding
13:403:31749:18:18:72:540:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function, so that the economy admits a unique ergodic distribution of types.  Uniqueness of
13:404:31840:18:18:72:380:116:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:optimal bids follows from a contraction mapping argument.5

14:410:32326:18:18:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by non-participation (a limitation we make precise below).  We think this is useful because
14:411:32417:18:18:72:540:581:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it makes explicit the assumptions that are needed to identify the primitives of the dynamic
14:412:32508:18:18:72:540:563:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:game.  Our result is constructive, so it also provides some guidance as to a sensible estimation
14:413:32604:18:24:72:116:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strategy.
14:414:32613:24:18:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  begin  with  a  scenario  in  which  the  econometrician  has  excellent  data  and  wishes  to
14:415:32712:18:18:72:540:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimate the baseline model of Section 2 (we investigate cases with limited data and more
14:416:32801:18:28:72:303:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complex demand models in Section 4 below).
14:417:32843:28:18:72:539:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Assumption  2(Observable  Data).In  every  auction,  the  econometrician  observes  the
14:418:32930:18:34:72:528:439:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:product-type being sold, all positive bids and the identities of the bidders that made them.
14:419:33022:34:18:72:540:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Even  in  this  case  we  assume  that  the  econometrician  does  not  observe  zero  bids,  since
14:420:33121:18:18:72:540:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those stand in for non-participation in our model (i.e.  non-participation is non-observable).
14:421:33215:18:18:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Despite this, identification of a number of components of the model follows directly.  First,
14:422:33308:18:18:72:539:351:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:{G1j}is directly observable from the data as the distribution of winning bids on each product.
14:423:33402:18:18:72:540:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  supply  transition  matrixQis  identified  by  the  probability  that  itemkis  auctioned
14:424:33496:18:24:72:156:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following itemj.
14:425:33512:24:18:71:540:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The activity rateτand survival probabilityrcannot be directly measured from the sample
14:426:33598:18:18:71:539:273:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analogs because some types will optimally choose to not participate even when active.  To
14:427:33687:18:18:71:540:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deal  with  this,  we  measureτandrfrom  a  sample  consisting  of  bidders  who  have  been
14:428:33779:18:18:71:539:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observed bidding on every product.  Such bidders have revealed themselves to be types that
14:429:33869:18:18:71:539:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will participate whenever active.  Define for each of these bidders a qualifying timet1i, the
14:430:33962:18:18:71:539:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time at which they qualified to be in this subset (i.e.  the time at which they bid on the last
14:431:34057:18:42:71:502:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remaining product they had not previously bid on).  Then for bidders in this sample
14:432:34140:42:32:128:540:141:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:r=P(bidder i is observed in any period> t1i|bidder lost in periodt1i)(3)
14:433:34212:32:21:72:94:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and,
14:434:34216:21:12:72:540:88:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:whom, for somej,βj(x) is neither zero nor interior toG1— i.e.  those who submit supXβj(x)— choose to
14:435:34316:12:0:71:212:76:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:bid something arbitrarily larger.
15:436:34351:0:32:130:540:653:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:rτ=P(bidder i is observed in periodt1i+ 1|bidder lost in periodt1i).(4)

15:448:34802:18:18:72:539:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Notice thatξ(b) is equal to the vector of of a buyer’s bids plus a second term that is equal
15:449:34894:18:18:72:540:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to their vector of continuation values.6There is a clear intuition for the second term:  when
15:450:34987:18:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a buyer wins with a bidbj, he gets a payoff equal to his value less the expected payment,

15:452:35163:18:18:72:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to his continuation value (Lemma 1 again, as he only wins ifbj>0), and so the payoff can

15:454:35341:18:18:72:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continuation value is thus equal in value to the stream of payments from a set ofJannuities,
15:455:35433:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where thejth paysG1(bj)(bj−E[B1j|B1j< bj]) in expectation wheneverjis auctioned.  The
15:456:35518:18:24:72:513:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pre-multiplication byr ̃Q(I−r ̃Q)−1sums the appropriate discounted geometric series.
15:457:35602:24:18:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In view of Lemma 1, this sum in (5) equal to the bidder’s value whenever the bid is positive,
15:458:35695:18:18:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:soξis an inverse bidding function on the regionb>0.  When components of the bid vector
15:459:35781:18:18:72:539:289:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:bare zero, however, we still obtain an upper bound on the bidder’s valuation.  Combining
15:460:35869:18:28:72:124:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this yields
15:461:35880:28:18:72:539:243:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Lemma 2(Bidder–wise Inversion).Letb=β(x).  Thenx≤ξ(b)with equality on every
15:462:35955:18:34:72:394:225:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:dimensionjsuch thatbj>0(i.e.x=ξ(b)ifbj>0for allj).
15:463:36005:34:18:72:539:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This result characterizes thebidder–wisecontent of data from an auction market.  Should
15:464:36092:18:18:72:540:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we observe a complete, strictly positive bid vector, it implies that we can exactly identify
15:465:36184:18:18:72:540:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bidder’s type.  In the particular case whereJ= 1, the inverse bidding function takes the
15:466:36276:18:18:72:135:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple form:
15:467:36288:18:0:201:253:119:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:ξ(b) =b+
15:468:36296:0:17:268:273:127:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:r
15:469:36297:17:0:257:283:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:?:1−r
15:470:36300:0:25:285:410:119:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:?:G1(b)(b−E[B1|B1< b])
15:471:36320:25:16:85:539:94:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:6The diligent reader can derive this expression by stacking the Bellman equations from (1) in vector form
15:472:36425:16:0:72:382:78:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:and then substituting in the optimal bidding strategies from Lemma 1.
16:473:36496:0:24:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the discrete-time analogue to the inverse bidding function in Hendricks and Sorensen (2014).
16:474:36588:24:18:72:540:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Given this inversion result, it will be helpful from now on to refer to the bid-vectorb≡β(x)
16:475:36680:18:18:71:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as  typex’s  “pseudo–type”.   Let  the  distribution  of  pseudo–types  be ̃F.   It  will  suffice  to
16:476:36782:18:18:71:539:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identify ̃Fto bound demandF. To see this, define a vector-valued indicator function 1(b>0)
16:477:36872:18:18:71:539:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with 1j(b>0) = 1 ifbj>0 and 1j(b>0) = 0 otherwise.  Then by Lemma 2,  we have
16:478:36949:18:33:71:474:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1(b)ξ(b)≤x≤ξ(b).  These pointwise inequalities translate into bounds onF:
16:479:37022:33:39:162:540:542:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f3:A:P({b:ξ(b)≤x})≤F(x)≤P({b: 1(b>0)ξ(b)≤x}).(6)
16:480:37065:39:18:71:539:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The missing part of our identification proof is a way of identifying the distribution of pseudo–
16:481:37161:18:18:71:539:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:types (and thus the probabilities on each side of the inequality in (6)).  With a single product,
16:482:37258:18:18:71:540:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this is a simple counting exercise: how many bidders are there who make each bidb(i.e. what
16:483:37349:18:18:71:540:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the bid distributionG(b))?  With multiple products this counting exercise is complicated
16:484:37440:18:24:71:539:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by selection, because most bidders will exit before placing a bid on every available product.
16:485:37533:24:18:71:539:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We deal with sample selection by choosing subsets of the data for which selection can be
16:486:37621:18:18:71:539:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:explicitly modeled and accounted for.  There are many such subsets one could construct in
16:487:37710:18:18:71:539:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:order to prove identification.  For example, one possible subset is the set of all complete bid
16:488:37805:18:18:71:539:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vectors.  The (joint) distribution of complete bids is observable, but selected:  pseudo–types
16:489:37899:18:18:71:540:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with highb1(e.g.)  will typically bid on product 1 and then win and exit, and therefore have
16:490:37991:18:24:71:371:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low density in the selected sample of complete bid vectors.
16:491:38050:24:18:71:539:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:One problem with this conditioning set is that there are many paths a bidder can take to make
16:492:38143:18:18:71:539:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a complete bid vector, and so calculating the probability of this event requires enumerating
16:493:38235:18:18:71:539:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and computing the probability of many paths.  So instead we work with the set of bidders
16:494:38323:18:18:71:540:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whose history falls into the following setH:  they enter when good 1 is available, bid, lose
16:495:38415:18:18:71:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  survive,  then  next  period  good  2  is  available,  and  the  bid,  lose  and  survive... Jis
16:496:38516:18:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:available, they bid, lose and survive.  Such bidders can be identified given the data available
16:497:38611:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:under Assumption 2.  Every pseudo–type who participates on every product is almost surely
16:498:38700:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:represented in this set, as every type on the interior of ̃Xcan lose an auction and survive to
16:499:38794:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bid on a different product.  We re-weight the observed frequency of pseudo–types observed
16:500:38883:18:18:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this subset by the inverse probability of inclusion– a selection correction that will allow us
16:501:38980:18:19:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to learn about the distribution of pseudo–types and, from (6), the distribution of types.  To
16:502:39073:19:18:72:540:94:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:compute the weights, we need to identify the probabilitysH(b) that a pseudo–typebends
16:503:39158:18:0:72:437:76:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:up in the setH, which is relatively straightforward for our choice ofH:
17:504:39231:0:34:72:516:671:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Lemma 3(Selection correction).Let Assumption 2 hold.  ThensH(b)is identified.
17:505:39308:34:18:72:540:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Let the joint density of their bids begH(b).  Lemma 3 allows us to re-weight the density
17:506:39396:18:33:72:344:619:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:gH(b) to get the density of pseudo–types withb>0:
17:507:39445:33:11:255:357:586:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f3:?: ̃f(b|b>0)∝gH(b)
17:508:39461:11:0:326:357:575:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:sH(b)
17:509:39466:0:42:525:540:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(7)
17:510:39469:42:18:72:540:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:But  this  only  characterizes  bidders  withb>0.   Revisiting  our  example  in  Figure  1(b),
17:511:39564:18:18:72:540:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidders of typesxandx′′are represented inH, but notx′, who never participates in auctions
17:512:39653:18:18:72:539:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:B:for  product  1.   Pseudo–types  that  don’t  participate  on  some  products  will  never  enterH
17:513:39751:18:18:72:540:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e.sH(b)  =  0),  and  so  to  move  from  the  conditional  distribution  to  the  unconditional
17:514:39850:18:18:72:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:B:distribution  takes  a  little  more  work.   The  idea  is  to  define  less  restrictive  setsH′⊃H
17:515:39950:18:18:72:540:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g.  sets of bidders who are observed bidding on product 1) and look for “extra mass” in
17:516:40040:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those  sets  generated  by  these  non-participating  pseudo–types.   In  the  appendix,  we  make
17:517:40138:18:18:72:540:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this argument formal, applying induction on the cardinality of the set of products each type
17:518:40230:18:28:72:540:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:participates in, starting from types who bid on every product.  Combining these arguments:
17:519:40320:28:18:72:539:369:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Theorem 2(Non-parametric identification).Let Assumption 2 hold.  Then ̃Fis point
17:520:40400:18:34:72:355:351:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:identified andFis partially identified, according to (6).
17:521:40457:34:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This  result  combines  the  bidder–wise  inversion  of  Lemma  2  with  the  selection  correction
17:522:40556:18:18:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:result of Lemma 3.  The dynamics of the auction market are important in both steps:  in the
17:523:40647:18:18:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first, the inverse bidding functionξ(·) captures bidders shading their bids by the option value
17:524:40742:18:18:72:540:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of losing and participating in future auctions;  in the second,sH(b) accounts for selection
17:525:40833:18:24:72:369:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into our sample, which is inherently dynamic whenJ >1.
17:526:40887:24:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  reason  that  Theorem  2  yields  partial  rather  than  complete  identification  is  that  we
17:527:40987:18:18:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allow  for  bidder  non-participation.   If  bidders  were  required  to  participate  (e.g.   primary
17:528:41089:18:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dealers  in  US  Treasury  auctions),  then  identification  would  be  exact.   Moreover,  we  note
17:529:41189:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that identification of our model is only incomplete in the left tail of the type distribution,
17:530:41283:18:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:precisely because it is driven by non-participation.  Our identification result is exact in the
17:531:41378:18:18:72:540:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:right tail, which is typically the relevant region for computing policy-relevant statistics, e.g.
17:532:41475:18:24:72:217:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:welfare or expected revenue.
17:533:41503:24:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, the proof and our exposition above hinged on a specially selected subset of bidders
17:534:41595:18:0:72:540:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with historyH.  We chose this subset for expositional clarity alone: though our identification
18:535:41691:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:argument is constructive, in practice we expect that the econometrician will be thoughtful
18:536:41781:18:18:72:540:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about which subsets — and therefore which variation in the data — to exploit in light of
18:537:41869:18:18:72:539:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their particular application.7In the same spirit, since the choice ofHwas expositional, so
18:538:41959:18:52:72:485:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:too is Lemma 3.  One could construct a similar argument for alternative subsets.
18:539:42039:52:35:72:192:565:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Extensions
18:540:42054:35:18:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In this we provide characterization and identification results for variations on the basic model.
18:541:42151:18:18:72:540:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We begin by showing that the model remains identified with data on only the winning and
18:542:42238:18:18:72:540:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:second  highest  bid  in  each  auction,  as  well  as  in  the  presence  of  reserve  prices.   We  also
18:543:42344:18:18:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show,  parallel  to  the  the  demand  estimation  literature  for  fixed  price  markets,  that  the
18:544:42445:18:18:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model is amendable to projection onto product characteristics, as in the random coefficient
18:545:42536:18:18:72:540:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:utility models of Berry et al. (1995).  We then generalize the model to a setting in which
18:546:42626:18:19:72:540:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there are additional state variables — beyond the product-type — that may affect bidder
18:547:42713:19:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:valuations and beliefs.  After characterizing bidding behavior in this case, we are also able to
18:548:42809:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show that the model remains non-parametrically identified in cases with unobserved product
18:549:42899:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneity and idiosyncratic payoff shocks.  Lastly, we consider a version of the model in
18:550:42992:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the presence of an unobserved, external fixed price market that agents may purchase from
18:551:43080:18:45:72:366:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instead of buying at auction, generating endogenous exit.
18:552:43137:45:31:72:203:286:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Limited Data
18:553:43156:31:18:72:540:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In many real world applications, the data does not contain all bids and identities.  Or even
18:554:43248:18:18:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if it does — as in our eBay application here — one may be concerned that not all bids are
18:555:43337:18:18:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:serious (in the sense that they are equal toβj(x)), and want to identify the model using data
18:556:43430:18:18:72:540:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only on the winning and second highest bid. Haile and Tamer (2003) offer a behavioral model
18:557:43521:18:18:72:540:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of ascending price auctions to motivate this concern,  and a number of  papers have taken
18:558:43610:18:18:72:540:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identification under this or similar data limitations seriously (Athey and Haile, 2002; Song,
18:559:43703:18:18:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2004; Menzel and Morganti, 2013; Platt, 2015) We consider the case where the econometrician
18:560:43794:18:18:72:507:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observes the two highest order statistics and show that the model remains identified.
18:561:43879:18:16:85:539:111:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:7This argument anticipates the illustrative empirical application of Section 5, where we choose to use only
18:562:43986:16:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:data for bidders who are observed bidding multiple times.  See in particular the discussion of the empirical
18:563:44094:12:0:72:164:83:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:design in Section 5.2.
19:564:44118:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Assumption 3(Limited Data).In each auction, the econometrician observes the product
19:565:44201:18:34:72:448:653:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:auctioned, the top two bids and the identities of the bidders placing them.
19:566:44276:34:18:72:539:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Lemma  2  still  applies,  so  identifying  ( ̃F,{G1j}j∈J,Q,r,τ)  is  sufficient  to  identifyξ(·)  and
19:567:44379:18:18:71:539:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:boundFaccording to (6).  The primitives{G1j}j∈JandQare still directly observable in the
19:568:44466:18:18:71:540:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data.  But now the difficulties in identifyingrandτwe had earlier are exacerbated by the
19:569:44554:18:18:71:539:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fact that a bidder will have (unobserved) gaps in their history whenever they were active but
19:570:44647:18:18:71:539:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:did not place one of the top two bids.  Our data is thus censored.  But since the probability
19:571:44740:18:18:71:539:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of being censored depends on the distribution of the second highest bids, which is observed,
19:572:44832:18:24:71:476:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the parametersτandrremain point identified (see the Appendix for a proof).
19:573:44906:24:18:71:540:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Thus the remaining problem is identifying the distribution of pseudo-types ̃Ffrom the ob-
19:574:44995:18:18:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:served  bidding  data.   Once  again,  we  can  think  of  this  as  a  selection  problem.   Consider
19:575:45097:18:18:71:540:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  subset  of  bidders  whose  history  falls  into  the  setH′(a  modified  version  ofH):  they
19:576:45196:18:18:71:539:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enter  when  good  1  is  available,make  the  second  highest  bid  (and  are  thus  observed),  then
19:577:45298:18:18:71:540:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:next period good 2 is available, theymake the second highest bid. . . goodJis available and
19:578:45389:18:18:72:539:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:theymake the second highest bid.  Since the event “make the second highest bid bidding on
19:579:45478:18:19:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:productj” is measurable with the data promised by Assumption 3,  these bidders can be
19:580:45563:19:18:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identified in the data.  And by similar arguments to those offered before, we can identify the
19:581:45657:18:28:72:433:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probabilitysH′(b) that we need for selection correction.  This gives us:
19:582:45729:28:18:72:539:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Theorem 3(Identification under Limited Data).Let  Assumption  3  hold.  ThenFis
19:583:45808:18:33:72:257:296:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:partially identified, according to (6).
19:584:45847:33:18:72:539:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For further intuition on this result, recall the discussion of our selection of the historyHat
19:585:45941:18:18:71:539:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the end of Section 3.  There are a number of possible histories on which we could have built
19:586:46033:18:19:71:539:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our identification result —Hwas an expository choice, butH′is also feasible.  As long as
19:587:46121:19:18:71:539:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the process by which bidders are selected into the sample can be recovered from observables,
19:588:46213:18:44:71:516:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our identification result is robust subject to the emendation of the selection correction.
19:589:46303:44:32:71:254:146:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    Random Coefficients
19:590:46329:32:18:71:539:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Let us suppose that the products have fixed (non-time-varying) characteristics, observable
19:591:46419:18:18:71:539:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the econometrician.  These are summarized in aJ×KmatrixZ, where the number of
19:592:46499:18:0:71:539:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characteristicsKis less than the number of productsJ.  We make two assumptions onZ:
20:593:46584:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that it is of full rank (this is necessary for identification), and that all entries are positive
20:594:46681:18:24:72:519:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(this is unnecessary but simplifies the analysis by allowing the inequality in (8) below).
20:595:46771:24:18:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Let bidderihave valuations of the formxi=Zαi, so that their preferences are summarized
20:596:46857:18:18:71:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by a random coefficientαi(aK×1 column vector).  Instead of sampling valuationsxupon
20:597:46940:18:18:72:540:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry fromF, we assume that bidders sample their random coefficientαfromFαinstead.
20:598:47022:18:24:72:306:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We would like to identify the distributionFα.
20:599:47067:24:18:72:540:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This demand structure is a special case of the model in which valuationsxcome from some
20:600:47154:18:18:72:539:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher-dimensional distributionF, and as a result optimal bidding and the inversion result
20:601:47244:18:33:72:519:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Lemma 2 remain unchanged.  We can boundFαusing the more general result in (6):
20:602:47325:33:33:149:540:482:12:g_d0_f12:12:g_d0_f3:A:P({b:ξ(b)≤Zα})≤Fα(α)≤P({b: 1(b>0)ξ(b)≤Zα})(8)
20:603:47370:33:18:72:539:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where we have simply replacedxin (6) byZα.  Intuitively, the probability that a random
20:604:47456:18:18:72:540:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coefficient is lower than some levelαis the same as the probability that the valuations are
20:605:47547:18:28:72:469:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower than the corresponding levelZα, and can be bounded in the same way.
20:606:47620:28:18:72:539:385:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Corollary 1(Identification under random coefficients).Suppose Assumption 3 holds.
20:607:47701:18:34:72:319:367:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:ThenFαis partially identified, according to (8).
20:608:47749:34:18:72:540:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Though the result is straightforward,  it highlights the generality of the type space of our
20:609:47841:18:18:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model from Section 2.  As in demand systems for fixed-price markets,  projection down to
20:610:47929:18:18:72:540:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:preferences over characteristic space yields dimension reduction.  Since we can partially iden-
20:611:48024:18:18:72:540:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tify a high-dimensional model with random preferences over products, we can also partially
20:612:48114:18:45:72:485:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identify a lower-dimensional model of random preferences for characteristics too.
20:613:48195:45:31:72:311:216:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.3    Demand with Richer Signals
20:614:48228:31:18:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now analyze a more substantial variation of the basic model in which we allow for both
20:615:48317:18:18:72:540:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:public  and  private  signals  that  affect  both  beliefs  and  valuations.   This  framework  is  the
20:616:48420:18:19:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:basis for two extensions:  public signals that affect beliefs about the state of the market and
20:617:48515:19:23:72:316:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unobserved heterogeneity in product attributes.
20:618:48562:23:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To accommodate this,  we need a richer state space.  Assume that in each period,  a state
20:619:48651:18:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables∈ Sis publicly observed.  This state variable may affect bidder valuations, so we
20:620:48741:18:0:72:540:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model a bidder’s valuation as a random functionxi(s).  Exactly howxi(s) is sampled will
21:621:48830:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depend on the specifics of the model.  For example, in the original model, the state variable
21:622:48923:18:18:72:539:653:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:B:was the product-type under auction (i.e.s∈ J), so valuations werexi(j)≡xi,jwherexi,j
21:623:49007:18:18:71:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:was thejth element ofxi, andxiwas sampled iid across biddersifromF.  The state variable
21:624:49094:18:28:71:513:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may also affect beliefs about competing bids, so we modify Assumption 1 accordingly:
21:625:49178:28:18:71:540:589:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Assumption 4(Beliefs with Public States).When the public state iss, bidders believe
21:626:49261:18:33:71:439:571:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:that the highest rival bid in the current auction has distributionG1(·|s).
21:627:49335:33:18:71:539:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For example, bidders may believe that when there is a lot of supply of a given good on the
21:628:49425:18:18:71:539:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market, the highest competing bid will be lower.  Assume also that bidders believe the state
21:629:49517:18:18:71:539:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transitions according to an exogenous Markov transition kernelP(s′|s) (exogenous in that
21:630:49605:18:27:71:347:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it is unaffected by the actions in the current auction).
21:631:49661:27:18:71:540:457:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:F:Definition 2(Equilibrium with Public States).A  pure  strategy  equilibrium  is  a  pair
21:632:49749:18:33:71:210:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:(βe(·,s),G1(·|s))such that:
21:633:49776:33:28:82:494:406:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:A:(Optimality)βe(x|s)is a best response for typexgiven beliefsG1(b|s)∀s∈S.
21:634:49848:28:33:73:304:378:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:(Consistency)G1(b|s) =μ([0,b]|s)∀s∈S.
21:635:49885:33:18:71:539:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Then by the same logic that we offered for Lemma 1, it is optimal for bidders to bid their
21:636:49975:18:28:71:407:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:valuation less their discounted continuation value, and we obtain:
21:637:50041:28:18:71:540:299:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Lemma 4(Best responses, general state space).The equilibrium bidding functionβ(s)
21:638:50122:18:19:71:114:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:satisfies:

21:648:50313:42:31:72:305:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.3.1    Public States and Bidder Beliefs
21:649:50354:31:18:72:540:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A special case of particular interest is whenS=J ×{s1,...,sS}andxi(s) =xi,j, i.e.  when
21:650:50441:18:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the state informs beliefs about competitor play, but does not encode valuation-relevant in-
21:651:50532:18:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formation.  We call attention to this not because it is technically demanding, but because
21:652:50622:18:0:72:540:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it  remedies  a  limitation  of  the  baseline  model:  that  it  misses  the  intuition  of  a  dynamic
22:653:50728:0:18:72:540:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marketplace in which bidders respond to changes in market fundamentals.  We can encode
22:654:50814:18:18:72:539:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:countably sophisticated information into the public state spaceS, including histories, chang-
22:655:50907:18:24:72:219:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing primitives, and foresight.
22:656:50937:24:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For instance,  suppose that bidders know not only what is being auctioned today,  but the
22:657:51026:18:18:72:539:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sequence  of  products  that  are  being  auctionedk−1  periods  into  the  future.   Then,S=
22:658:51119:18:18:72:540:575:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:Jk,  and  bidders’  continuation  values  will  now  depend  upon  realizations  of  future  supply.
22:659:51219:18:18:72:540:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Alternatively, suppose thatτ, the re-arrival rate of bidders, evolves over{τL,τH}in a public
22:660:51311:18:18:72:539:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Markov process.  Now,S=J×{τL,τH}.  In theτHworld bidders face more competition
22:661:51393:18:24:71:436:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from more bidders, and so it is useful to let this be reflected inG1(·|s).
22:662:51467:24:18:71:539:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:It is straightforward to see that this presents no theoretical difficulty for identification.  The
22:663:51565:18:18:71:539:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simplest approach is by brute force application of Theorem 2:  simply define ̃Jto contain
22:664:51654:18:18:71:540:461:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:B:|S|duplicates of the product spaceJand proceed as before.  It is also possible to show,
22:665:51741:18:18:71:540:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using a contraction mapping argument, that the fullJ×|S|bid vector is identified from any
22:666:51830:18:41:71:336:425:12:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f5:C:J-vector that includes a bid for each product type.8
22:667:51882:41:31:72:420:384:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.3.2    Unobserved Heterogeneity and Idiosyncratic Shocks
22:668:51940:31:18:72:540:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  introduce  a  variant  of  the  model  with  unobserved  product  heterogeneity  and  id-
22:669:52038:18:18:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:iosyncratic taste shocks (this will be useful in the application).  In this setting unobserved
22:670:52132:18:18:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:product heterogeneity (ξt) is public and transient, and idiosyncratic taste shocks (εi,t) are
22:671:52225:18:33:72:348:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:private and transient.  We assume that valuations are:
